  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1623186073070350906">The acclaimed <i>Farseer</i> and <i>Liveship Traders</i> trilogies established Robin Hobb as one of the most splendidly imaginative practitioners of world-class fantasy. <br/><br/>Now, in Book 2 of her most stunning trilogy yet, Hobb continues the soul-shattering tale of FitzChivalry Farseer. With rich characters, breathtaking magic, and sweeping action, <b>Golden Fool</b> brings the reluctant adventure</span>
  <span id="freeText1623186073070350906" style="display:none">The acclaimed <i>Farseer</i> and <i>Liveship Traders</i> trilogies established Robin Hobb as one of the most splendidly imaginative practitioners of world-class fantasy. <br /><br />Now, in Book 2 of her most stunning trilogy yet, Hobb continues the soul-shattering tale of FitzChivalry Farseer. With rich characters, breathtaking magic, and sweeping action, <b>Golden Fool</b> brings the reluctant adventurer further into the fray in an epic of sacrifice, salvation, and untold treachery.<br /><br /><b>Golden Fool<br /><br /></b>Prince Dutiful has been rescued from his Piebald kidnappers and the court has resumed its normal rhythms. But for FitzChivalry Farseer, a return to isolation is impossible. Though gutted by the loss of his wolf bondmate, Nighteyes, Fitz must take up residence at Buckkeep and resume his tasks as Chade’s apprentice assassin. Posing as Tom Badgerlock, bodyguard to Lord Golden, FitzChivalry becomes the eyes and ears behind the walls. And with his old mentor failing visibly, Fitz is forced to take on more burdens as he attempts to guide a kingdom straying closer to civil strife each day.<br /><br />The problems are legion. Prince Dutiful’s betrothal to the Narcheska Elliania of the Out Islands is fraught with tension, and the Narcheska herself appears to be hiding an array of secrets. Then, amid Piebald threats and the increasing persecution of the Witted, FitzChivalry must ensure that no one betrays the Prince’s secret—a secret that could topple the Farseer throne: that he, like Fitz, possesses the dread “beast magic.”<br /><br />Meanwhile, FitzChivalry must impart to the Prince his limited knowledge of the Skill: the hereditary and addictive magic of the Farseers. In the process, they discover within Buckkeep one who has a wild and powerful talent for it, and whose enmity for Fitz may have disastrous consequences for all.<br /><br />Only Fitz’s enduring friendship with the Fool brings him any solace. But even that is shattered when unexpected visitors from Bingtown reveal devastating secrets from the Fool’s past. Now, bereft of support and adrift in intrigue, Fitz’s biggest challenge may be simply to survive the inescapable and violent path that fate has laid out for him.<br /><br /><br /><i>From the Hardcover edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1623186073070350906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3393780316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6544552755441910379"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12479390.The_Golden_Fool__Tawny_Man___2_' title='The Golden Fool (Tawny Man, #2) by Robin Hobb' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Golden Fool</a><b> (Realm of Elderlings #8, Tawny Man #2)</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586154514ra/29239410.gif' width='480' height='238' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Definitely start with the Farseer Trilogy series, and the Liveship Traders before reading the Tawny Man series because somehow Hobb manages to weave this ever-growing world together gorgeously, making it appear natural and effortless. You will have a much richer appreciation of what is going on if you read everything in the written order.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>It's all connected. When you save any part of the world, you've saved the whole world. In fact, that's </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6544552755441910379" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12479390.The_Golden_Fool__Tawny_Man___2_" title="The Golden Fool (Tawny Man, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">The Golden Fool</a><b> (Realm of Elderlings #8, Tawny Man #2)</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586154514ra/29239410.gif" width="480" height="238" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Definitely start with the Farseer Trilogy series, and the Liveship Traders before reading the Tawny Man series because somehow Hobb manages to weave this ever-growing world together gorgeously, making it appear natural and effortless. You will have a much richer appreciation of what is going on if you read everything in the written order.<br><blockquote>
  <i>It's all connected. When you save any part of the world, you've saved the whole world. In fact, that's the only way it can be done.</i>
</blockquote><br><i>Fascinating writing.</i></span>

<div id="review_1830295618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830295618" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830295618?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007585908" href="/book/show/23018984-the-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830295618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14566513999189456334"><b>This was almost another 5 stars read, this was almost as good as Fool’s Errand, but it wasn’t due to the second book syndrome that is quite evident here.</b><br/><br/>The Golden Fool is almost completely a preparation and transition book for the big conclusion in the next installment. It’s all about laying foundations and moving the characters to have the right convictions and motivation to save the world. Though, knowing Fitz, he’ll probably brood about it still. Because of this plot direction, there’s close</span>
  <span id="freeText14566513999189456334" style="display:none"><b>This was almost another 5 stars read, this was almost as good as Fool’s Errand, but it wasn’t due to the second book syndrome that is quite evident here.</b><br><br>The Golden Fool is almost completely a preparation and transition book for the big conclusion in the next installment. It’s all about laying foundations and moving the characters to have the right convictions and motivation to save the world. Though, knowing Fitz, he’ll probably brood about it still. Because of this plot direction, there’s close to nothing going on in the book plot-wise even though it’s more than 600 pages long. Overall, I don’t mind this. As far as a transitional book goes, The Golden Fool is still great.<br><br>The problems that I had with the book were actually on the first 200 pages. I struggled heavily with this part. It was boring at parts and it seemed completely directionless. Plus, the last three chapters were quite anti-climatic, and Starling seriously need to be cut off from this series already. These are really the only parts I disliked about this book.<br><br>The book picked up its pace for me once the story entered chapter 11, where a few characters from Liveship Traders trilogy appeared for a while. Starting from chapter 11, the book became wonderful to me up until the end. I was overjoyed by this crossover, it goes to show that Hobb has really created a fantastic cast of characters within all her books. Whether it’s the characters from Farseer, Liveship or Tawny Man trilogy, all of them are extremely well-written. Although it took like 200 pages to get to, it was truly worth it.<br><br>Not only these crossovers were incredible because of the characters, it also shows just how great Hobb is at world-building her the entirety of her series. The world-building keeps on improving, filled with rich lore about the Skill and the Wit, also more revelations about the dragons, the Elderlings, and every information the readers accumulated from both Farseer and Liveship do play a part here. Hobb seamlessly connects the events in Liveship Traders into Fitz’s storyline, which make Liveship a mandatory read in order to get more satisfaction out of this book and trilogy.<br><br> <b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We are the sum of all we have done added to the sum of all that has been done to us.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>There aren’t a lot of things left to say on this review about this book. The story continued immediately from where it left off in Fool’s Errand and the entire setting of the book took place in Buckkeep. The majority of the book was spent on Buckkeep politics, the mastery of skills, and Fitz’s interactions with all the other characters. Some of my absolute favorite parts from this book was the forming of the coterie, every characters' development, some revelations on The Fool’s past, and the complexity of Fitz relationship with him.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Love is more than bedding, boy. If love doesn't come first and linger after, if love can't wait and endure disappointment and separation, then it's not love. Love doesn't require bedding to make it true. It doesn't even demand day to day contact. I know this because I have known love."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Overall, The Golden Fool is a transitional book and despite having some issues with it, I still love this. Tawny Man has been really solid so far and I hope Hobb can deliver the satisfying conclusion that this trilogy needs in Fool’s Fate, the book that the majority of Hobb’s fans are claiming to be her best work.<br><br><b>Picture: <i>The Golden Fool</i> by Yasushi Suzuki</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519559662i/25120234._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>You can find <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/pat/1062-thegoldenfool" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></b> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <b><a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14566513999189456334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1129822407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129822407" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129822407?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007585908" href="/book/show/23018984-the-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129822407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15069386044501415798">Fitz is in a bad way, and it’s not surprising considering what happened at the end of the last novel. We all knew it was coming eventually, but I honestly didn’t expect it so soon. I guess age finally catches up with us all. But for Fitz, he has lost half his soul; he will never be quite the same again. <br/><br/><b> Is this an excuse to finally return? </b><br/><br/>What his loss has granted him is loneliness. And this forces him back into an old life. He picks up the old tools of the trade, his axe and his poisons: he r</span>
  <span id="freeText15069386044501415798" style="display:none">Fitz is in a bad way, and it’s not surprising considering what happened at the end of the last novel. We all knew it was coming eventually, but I honestly didn’t expect it so soon. I guess age finally catches up with us all. But for Fitz, he has lost half his soul; he will never be quite the same again. <br><br><b> Is this an excuse to finally return? </b><br><br>What his loss has granted him is loneliness. And this forces him back into an old life. He picks up the old tools of the trade, his axe and his poisons: he returns to Buckeep castle once more, the place he grew up in. He takes solace in the companionship of old friends, but that’s not why he returned, he returned because he needed distraction: he needed an excuse to move on with his life. And the mysterious politics of the Farseer reign is the perfect thing to immerse himself in once more. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386617876i/7406129._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As ever, the Six Duchies are plagued with strife and tension. This time the cause is a tenuous marriage contract, one that will only be fulfilled if King Dutiful brings back his betrothed the head of a dragon. Yes, a dragon’s head. This is not an easy task. Dragons are powerful creatures, but they’re also vertically extinct, so, needless to say, more problems arise. Fitz’s oldest friend, the Fool, wishes to revive the dragons not slay them. Fitz is stuck in the middle. His duty to his King demands he helps in the perilous quest, and his loyalty to his friend demands he helps to preserve dragonkind. He has some rather tricky decisions to make. <br><br><b> Slow, slow, character development</b><br><br>Like all of Robin Hobb books this is incredibly drawn out, wonderfully so. Hundreds of pages fly by, in which little progress is made, but in this resides the beauty of Robin Hobb’s style. She doesn’t rush. She takes her time. She allows the tension to build up until it eventually erupts in a most dramatic manner. The slowness of her books to many is a flaw but to me it’s wonderful. If a writer can pull you along in a story, in which the characters spend large amounts of time lamenting over the past, and yet you don’t get bored with the words, you know she is doing something right. I could read about Fitz and the Fool all day. <br><br>Fitz has grown very gradually over this series, and he still has, no doubt, much further to go. I think the loss he has sustained has made him much stronger. He has come to rely on his other form of magic, and even has gained his own group of telepathically linked individuals. The student has become the master. I loved his relationship with Thick, the mentally deficient, yet extremely powerful, skill user. The Fitz in the first series wouldn’t have had the wisdom to deal with him in such a kindly efficient manner. <br><br><b>A great book!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15069386044501415798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2314723952" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2314723952" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2314723952?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31839482-the-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2314723952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3921453747616344976"><b>
  <i>One man armed with the right word may do what an army of swordsmen cannot.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Golden Fool is the second book in the Tawny Man Trilogy, this book didn't exactly suffer from middle book syndrome, it's more like the author used this book as a preparation for the third book, Golden Fool just set things in place for what would happen in the final book.<br/><br/>Just how a preparation for a journey is as important as the journey itself, that's what this book is to the series. There are lots of factors in this b</span>
  <span id="freeText3921453747616344976" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>One man armed with the right word may do what an army of swordsmen cannot.</i>
</b><br /><br />Golden Fool is the second book in the Tawny Man Trilogy, this book didn't exactly suffer from middle book syndrome, it's more like the author used this book as a preparation for the third book, Golden Fool just set things in place for what would happen in the final book.<br /><br />Just how a preparation for a journey is as important as the journey itself, that's what this book is to the series. There are lots of factors in this book that I love, some of which are friendship, great characters, awesome writing, unique plot, and a visit from another series( some characters from Bingtown were in this, they gave an in-depth update on what is happening with everyone. <br /><br />The writing style is the best thing about this author's work, the writing somehow swoops you into the book, I feel like I'm one of the characters instead of an outside observer. There are very few authors who writes as good as she does. This book is written solely from Fitz's perspective. The world building is as good as the writing.<br /><br />Golden Fool started from where Fool's Errand ended, Fitz is back to Buckeep posing as Lord Golden's servant. While in the background he is teaching Dutiful the skill and working as a spy for Chade. The betrothal with Elliana was going well or so they thought till she demanded he kill a dragon frozen in ice for centuries as a sign of his prowess. The Piebald are back, the negotiations with the Old Blood are still ongoing, lots of other little things also took place in this.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>To recognize you are the source of your own loneliness is not a cure for it. But it is a step towards seeing that it is not inevitable, and that such a choice is not irrevocable.</i>
</b><br /><br />The above quote is from Fitz, I love that he is finally realizing that he is to blame for some of his problems. I'm really loving grown-up him not that I didn't like him in Farseer but he is much more matured here. I love how he's handling his relationship with Dutiful, it's quite admirable. He is still as loyal as before but every now and then he stands up for himself which is progress.<br /><br />Lord Golden wasn't in this as much as I wanted, he was barely in the second half of the book. He is still as mysterious as ever, I think that is due to the fact that Fitz the narrator only knows what Golden shows. There were times when he shows almost no glimpse of The Fool, how does he do it and what is his gender. One thing is for sure, he loves Fitz, I just hope that it's enough.<br /><br />Dutiful just keeps surprising me, how can he a prince be this kind and humble. Whenever I read about him, it makes me so proud of Kettricken. Dutiful is taking his lessons so well, he's still somewhat obsessed with Fitz, he all but hangs on his every word. Despite his respect for Fitz he is still his own person. He does things that even Fitz won't approve of that he thinks is good. He is ready to apologize if he does something wrong.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Love is more than bedding, boy. If love doesn’t come first and linger after, if love can’t wait and endure disappointment and separation, then it’s not love. Love doesn’t require bedding to make it true. It doesn’t even demand day to day contact. I know this because I have known love, many kinds of loves, and among them, I’ve known what I felt for you.’</i>
</b><br /><br />Hap was a mess at the first half of the book, I liked that. Mistakes helps us become a better us. He realises his mistake and turned on a new leaf, I just hopes it last.<br /><br />Kettricken is finally becoming her own Queen, she all but let Chade rule before but now she has taken the reins, he normally disagrees with her but that does not stop her from doing what she thinks is right.<br /><br />Elliana is a character that I can't wait to see more of, she is just twelve but has a making of a strong character. I hope there is more of her in the next book.<br /><br />Thick is a simpleton and a servant at Buckeep, he is also very strong in the skill, Civil, Swift and Web are other characters that I'm looking forward to reading about in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3921453747616344976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1327238374" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1327238374" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1327238374?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780002247276" href="/book/show/2399033.The_Golden_Fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327238374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3144215450654284750">What is this book...? Well, it's the continuation of Fitz's storyline. It's also the continuation of the Fool's storyline and Bukkeep's storyline. I would also go so far as to say that this is the continuation of the Elderlings world. This book, although focused on Fitz most of the time, is actually a story which traverses the boundaries of the two series we've previously read in this world. Whilst before now we have had small easter egg references to events or people within one of the other ser</span>
  <span id="freeText3144215450654284750" style="display:none">What is this book...? Well, it's the continuation of Fitz's storyline. It's also the continuation of the Fool's storyline and Bukkeep's storyline. I would also go so far as to say that this is the continuation of the Elderlings world. This book, although focused on Fitz most of the time, is actually a story which traverses the boundaries of the two series we've previously read in this world. Whilst before now we have had small easter egg references to events or people within one of the other series books, we've not had a big crossover of many characters or events which directly affect the story quite as much. We get to see the return of some of those we met in Liveships, and we also see or hear about how many of the lives of those we enjoyed from the Farseer books are going. We meet new people along the way too, of course, but mainly this book felt to me like the beginning of a solidified narrative between all 8 of the books so far in the Realm of the Elderlings.<br /><br />This story follows Fitz after his return to the mysteries and struggles at Bukkeep court. We can see the many challenges his return has forced him to face, and we see many old and new faces who are, inevitably, mixed up in his storyline too. We get to follow Fitz through yet more ups and down, some of which were shocking, others seemingly destined, and we see how he copes against those who wish him harm and the secrets he must keep.<br /><br />One element of this book I particularly enjoyed were the italicised passages at the beginning of each chapter. Whilst I have thought that these were always interesting I think some of those shown within this book in particular have been most insightful and enlightening.<br /><br />I also really liked getting to see more of the characters of Dutiful, Thick, Hap and the Narcheska (alongside, of course, Fitz and the Fool) because each one was uniquely interesting and full of life and vibrance in their own way. <br />We see Dutiful trying to become the man he strives to be and fill his position at Bukkeep well. <br />We get to see Thick, a new character who is a halfwit, as he struggles against much of the same adversity and cruelty that Fitz had been subjected to in the past. <br />We see Hap as he comes up against some of the fancies and ideals that young men around town are prone to and falls into some pitfalls which lead him to make his own mistakes.<br />And finally we learn a little more about the Narcheska herself and her, rather odd and foreign, country which is maybe not so different to Buck. <br />Each of these characters either amused me, intrigued me or made me worry for the at some point in the story meaning that I was constantly invested in their stories and what would happen next. I felt that the changing story threads for each of the characters was handled expertly and each one was given proper time to develop and unfold as Hobb intended.<br /><br />On the whole the story of this one was great and featured some excellent and central moments which will no doubt change the path of the next book and the history of Buck forever more. I cannot wait to finish up the Tawny Man series and see what is happening, and I also thought that this was one of the first times that I think the third book might be the best because of how much stuff Hobb has set in motion which will have to be resolved in book 3.<br /><br />I cannot wait for the final one, this one was a wonderful 5*s with some excellent writing and fab story-telling!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3144215450654284750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2452835800" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2452835800" />
    <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books"><img alt="Em Lost In Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522743986p2/11166121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2452835800?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em Lost In Books" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books">Em Lost In Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6392157-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2000-09">2000-09</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=massive-tomes">massive-tomes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2452835800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3889556974989906850"><b>
  <i>“You seek a false comfort when you demand that I define myself for you with words. Words do not contain or define any person. A heart can, if it is willing.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Robin Hobb certainly knows how to spin a tale. I was rapt with her words, even though Fitz was drowning himself in pity and remorse. I was still turning pages when Fitz was planning (only planning) to kill all and get over with this ordeal. I finished the book and said wow, this was fantastic. That’s how magical her tales are.<br/><br/>I know I di</span>
  <span id="freeText3889556974989906850" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“You seek a false comfort when you demand that I define myself for you with words. Words do not contain or define any person. A heart can, if it is willing.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Robin Hobb certainly knows how to spin a tale. I was rapt with her words, even though Fitz was drowning himself in pity and remorse. I was still turning pages when Fitz was planning (only planning) to kill all and get over with this ordeal. I finished the book and said wow, this was fantastic. That’s how magical her tales are.<br /><br />I know I didn’t like Assassin’s Quest much. I was as frustrated as Fitz was throughout the book by the time finished reading it. This book too doesn’t offer in terms of action, adventure, or drama, and yet it was beautiful to read Fitz’s struggle with loss and betrayal. I think Ms Hobb has grown on me and that’s why I am loving this tale now instead of whining and cursing. <br /><br /> This being the middle book paved path for the journey that we will read about in next book. Hobb threw in some mystery/mythical elements to make it more attractive and I am more than ready to start that journey to slay some dragons.<br /><br />But this book has its moments. I loved the Court politics and how Kettricken was trying to win the alliances. While Dutiful was certainly not a favourite character in the last book, here he definitely holds his own. He was humble, eager to learn, possessive of Fitz, and a very brave young lad, who didn’t like being thought of as a stupid prince. <br /><br />Book’s highlight for me was relationship of Fitz and Fool. It’s the first time I have seen such strife between the two. I certainly missed few things as I have not read LivShip Traders, but Hobb wrote their conflict with so much emotion that it was painful for me to read those pages. <br /><br />It was a great story but also tests the patience of readers. As for me, I will be going on adventure with Fool and Fitz next month to see what future holds for these two. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3889556974989906850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText739097818702728794" style="display:none">I can't say this is my favorite Robin Hobb book, but that is like saying it is not my favorite type of chocolate. It's still fucking delicious.<br /><br />I just felt that this one dragged a bit more and while a lot happened there was really no resolution. It is the second book in a trilogy, but in the first book I felt like things were accomplished even though it was nowhere near the end.<br /><br />Then I started this and so many plots were set into motion that I'm not sure how she can wrap them all up in one more book. But that is all that this book did was set things into motion. I am excited to see where those things lead for sure, I just wish this book either resolved SOMETHING, or was a tad bit shorter. (Blasphemy I know!)</span>

<div id="review_713644972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713644972" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713644972?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006486022" href="/book/show/6662425-the-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713644972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16282913008944166855">I'm enjoying this Trilogy so far even more than the previous two in the series. Robin Hobb's writing is either getting better or I am just increasingly more invested in the characters of her world - probably both. Either way, Hobb's characterization is second to none. She can make you feel the joy of friendship rekindled or the rift of a lover's quarrel or the grief that come's with a close companion's death. <i>Let us now pause a moment to remember NightEyes...</i><br/><br/>The other thing that made this book v</span>
  <span id="freeText16282913008944166855" style="display:none">I'm enjoying this Trilogy so far even more than the previous two in the series. Robin Hobb's writing is either getting better or I am just increasingly more invested in the characters of her world - probably both. Either way, Hobb's characterization is second to none. She can make you feel the joy of friendship rekindled or the rift of a lover's quarrel or the grief that come's with a close companion's death. <i>Let us now pause a moment to remember NightEyes...</i><br /><br />The other thing that made this book very enjoyable was the audio narration by Nick Taylor. Somehow he just nailed exactly how I imagine certain character's voices in my head. Namely Fitz, the Fool, and Chade. On the other hand the French accents for Kettricken and Dutiful were a stroke of genius and now I can't imagine them sounding any other way.<br /><br />Our story picks up right after the events of book one. On the surface of things the plot takes a step back, slowing right down as Fitz reconnects with his old life at Buck Keep. Some relationships are renewed while others are deliberately avoided. Fitz' foster son, Hap, is settled into a trade apprenticeship in Buck Town. Fitz explores his relationship with the hedgewitch Jinna. Fitz establishes his cover as Tom Badgelock, Lord Golden's serving man come bodyguard. Nothing much appears to be happening plot wise. Yet Robin Hobb has that ability to make the simple pleasures of walking through Buck Town or raiding the kitchens of the Keep such delightful experiences, recalling fond memories of Fitz' childhood and coming of age in the Farseer Trilogy. <br /><br />I'm making it sound boring but it's not really. Part of the reason why those moments are to be treasured is because they are snippets of light that stand out in stark contrast to the darker undertones and more sinister intrigues permeating the story. And though the pace may seem to have slowed down in some regards it actually hurtles forward in other ways. There was no point where I was bored or felt the story was getting bogged down and needed to move along. There is actually a lot going on. Fitz has so much to deal with he doesn't have time to scratch himself. <br /><br />In the Farseer Trilogy Fitz role was well defined as the Assassins Apprentice. This time he is no longer Chade's apprentice and his role is a lot more fluid as he is thrown back into the intrigues of the Six Duchies and court of Buck Keep. This time he returns as The Skillmaster, assigned to assemble and train a coterie of skill users for Prince Dutiful - even though his own Skill training was limited and twisted and he has nearly as much to learn as his students. <br /><br />When he's not doing that he is a royal Spymaster - assigned to dig out secrets while keeping his own and the crown's well covered. And yes, if the need should arise, he will again assume the role of Royal Assassin. Whenever problems arise, killing is always on the table as an option, whether the problem be a simpleton who knows too much or Piebalds lurking somewhere in town. <br /><br />And Fitz has all his old Assassin's tools honed and ready to use - whether it be foresight to be able to avoid violence altogether - or ruthless pragmatism combined with herbal lore to inflict death by food poisoning - or whether it be cold steel when gutting one's enemy is all that's left to do.<br /><br /><br />5 stars<br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Warning</b>
</u><br /><i>Fitz will be subjected to extreme harm during the course of this story. Fitz lovers are advised to consider using the dead tree edition of this book in preference to electronic devices that are vulnerable to shock damage. Be also advised that no characters in the book are able to hear you no matter how hard you yell at the pages. If you must yell and are using an electronic device take care to cover any exposed ports as device manufacturers generally don't provide warranty for moisture damage.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16282913008944166855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1537376436?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1537376436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12339455384895548197">If you like fast pacing and high action, walk away! This story introduces one of my favourite characters, Thick, a ‘dim-wit ‘ serving boy who becomes an essential part of Dutiful’s coterie. As always with Hobb’s writing, the deep, thoughtful details and awareness of the human psyche are an invaluable part of her books. It pained my heart to see the Fool and Fitz so out of sync in this one. I love that Fitz, our ‘hero’ is no hero and makes many mistakes and missteps and yet tries to do the right </span>
  <span id="freeText12339455384895548197" style="display:none">If you like fast pacing and high action, walk away! This story introduces one of my favourite characters, Thick, a ‘dim-wit ‘ serving boy who becomes an essential part of Dutiful’s coterie. As always with Hobb’s writing, the deep, thoughtful details and awareness of the human psyche are an invaluable part of her books. It pained my heart to see the Fool and Fitz so out of sync in this one. I love that Fitz, our ‘hero’ is no hero and makes many mistakes and missteps and yet tries to do the right thing. His role as catalyst seems particularly well defined in this book. Recommended, but you need to be prepared for the long haul for the whole of the Realm of the Elderlings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12339455384895548197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2310999116" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2310999116" />
    <a title="Lema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18145934-lema"><img alt="Lema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507843225p2/18145934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2310999116?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lema" href="/user/show/18145934-lema">Lema</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007585908" href="/book/show/23018984-the-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2310999116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9701156490567644984"><b>If I want to approach this book in a subjective way, I would say it definitely is a filler and a set up for events to come. If I want to approach it realistically from a point of view of someone who had invested so much time and effort (AND FEELS) into this series, then I have to say that this book gave me life (AND FEELS) and I enjoyed every single second of it.</b><br/><br/>I'm lazy as eff and I immediately started Fool's Fate because IM WEAK AND NEED TO KNOW WHAT HAPPENS WITH MA BABIES, so this is will be </span>
  <span id="freeText9701156490567644984" style="display:none"><b>If I want to approach this book in a subjective way, I would say it definitely is a filler and a set up for events to come. If I want to approach it realistically from a point of view of someone who had invested so much time and effort (AND FEELS) into this series, then I have to say that this book gave me life (AND FEELS) and I enjoyed every single second of it.</b><br><br>I'm lazy as eff and I immediately started Fool's Fate because IM WEAK AND NEED TO KNOW WHAT HAPPENS WITH MA BABIES, so this is will be brief.<br>I could never imagine someone writing day-to-day life and make it not boring as masterfully as Robin Hobb did in this book. My favorite setting so far in the Realm of the Elderlings -despite all of the exotic places that we visited- has got to be Buckkeep and Bucktown. I don't know call me nostalgic but just reading the description of that place give me all the fuzzies and warm feelings. So when I saw that Golden Fool was mostly set there, I didn't even care that nothing else was happening except following the daily lives of our characters, why do you ask? Because of this lovely thing called Character Development.<br><br><b>
  <i>“You seek a false comfort when you demand that I define myself for you with words. Words do not contain or define any person. A heart can, if it is willing.”</i>
</b><br><br>Oh and Hobb's prose, did I mention how glorious it's becoming?<br>The combination of the massive character growth along with Hobb's magical writing made this book a fantastical experience for me, it's thought provoking, emotional, touching, mysterious and overall unforgettable. Not to mention that I have never read about a character with Down Syndrome before in fantasy, I'm still not sure how I feel about the character itself, but I thought it was an admirable and intriguing inclusion to a wide cast of wonderful and diverse characters.<br>I'm at this point currently where I'm just thankful that I have this series in my life :')<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508756432ra/24250353.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fool's Fate here I come! pleasebegoodpleasebegoodpleasebegoodpleasebegood..<br><br>1. Fool's Errand: 5 Stars (here's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2304075502" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a>)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3127861592998888593">This book was good, but for the most part I felt like it was just filling in the story between the first and the third book in this Tawny Man trilogy. Not a lot happens, and everything is a build-up to the big adventure we will encounter in book three.<br/>I wasn't at any point eager to get back to this book and read it, but when I did read I liked it because it is entertaining and in many ways thought-provoking. Fitz is a likeable man, and that goes for almost all of the other characters as well. <br/>So</span>
  <span id="freeText3127861592998888593" style="display:none">This book was good, but for the most part I felt like it was just filling in the story between the first and the third book in this Tawny Man trilogy. Not a lot happens, and everything is a build-up to the big adventure we will encounter in book three.<br />I wasn't at any point eager to get back to this book and read it, but when I did read I liked it because it is entertaining and in many ways thought-provoking. Fitz is a likeable man, and that goes for almost all of the other characters as well. <br />So while it wasn't my favourite of Robin Hobb's, it was still an enjoyable read that however left me somewhat bored through parts of it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7994512800537571149">Here we are again, the middle book of a Hobb trilogy. I really think she hits her stride in these second books. The pace has built up a bit from the first, and it sets up the third one nicely. <br/><br/>There were a couple of emotional scenes in this that are certainly appreciated by a long time reader of this overall series. I won't go into it, but they alone made this book something special. I hope they are a good preview of what's to come in Book #3, which I'll be starting soon.</span>

          </span>

        <a title="Michelle Morrell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Morrell" href="/user/show/127000-michelle-morrell">Michelle Morrell</a>

        rated it

So crazily well written it hurts.<br/><br/>My only complaint is people in this book need to stop concerning themselves about what goes on in two consenting adults's bedchambers. Evolve already!</span>

<div id="review_1984008078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984008078" />
    <a title="Phee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26480778-phee"><img alt="Phee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580467651p2/26480778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984008078?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phee" href="/user/show/26480778-phee">Phee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007585908" href="/book/show/23018984-the-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26480778-phee?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1984008078&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984008078" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12319322312584607041">Right then. Firstly, this isn't really going to be a proper review. All the Realm of the Elderlings books that I have read to this point have been unique, well written and have impressed me. This one is no different and I would hate to sound like a broken record. Also if your looking at reviews for this book then you should already know by now how good Hobb is at grand stories, real characters and character development, and tormenting the reader with a fantastic plot. <br/>If your looking at reviews </span>
  <span id="freeText12319322312584607041" style="display:none">Right then. Firstly, this isn't really going to be a proper review. All the Realm of the Elderlings books that I have read to this point have been unique, well written and have impressed me. This one is no different and I would hate to sound like a broken record. Also if your looking at reviews for this book then you should already know by now how good Hobb is at grand stories, real characters and character development, and tormenting the reader with a fantastic plot. <br />If your looking at reviews for this book and you've not read any of the previous books then leave this review and read Assassins Apprentice right away. <br /> <br />This is going to be my overall thoughts and may be a little bit of a ramble. I am incredibly passionate about these books and more importantly the characters of Fitz and the Fool. <br /><br />One major thing that annoyed me with this book was that on the back of the edition that I read (uk cover) it mentions the quest to go and kill the dragon Icefyre. The way it is worded suggests that it would be the main plot point for this book. However they do not even leave to go this quest by the end of the book. A little misleading in my opinion. <br /><br />Now to the good stuff. <br />This book was definitely where we learn so much more about the Fool. One of the characters from the Liveship traders Amber is revealed to have been the Fool in disguise. Something that didn't shock me as I had worked it out long ago but I'm sure that some people may not have noticed all the hints in the Liveship books to Amber's real identity. <br />We also learn a lot more about Fitz, or maybe I should say that Fitz learns a lot more about himself. I must say that I am proud of the man that Fitz has become and the way he has brought up Hap. <br /><br />Now the really good stuff. <br />A big part as to why this book was so good was the way it played with my emotions. Fitz and the Fool have a very big argument in this book. It changes their relationship in a major way and I'm certain that the they will always remember what was spoken in that argument. <br />The Fool has always told Fitz that he loves him. He told him in Assassins Quest, and Fitz has always said that he loves the Fool also, but how one loves a brother, not romantically. However quite a few events in this book lead too Fitz asking the Fool the true intent of his love. When he asks, Fitz is drinking elfbark which always dampens his spirits and makes him irritable. The Fool is also unwell due to the changes that his kind undergo every now and then, although this is not known to Fitz at the time, I think this effects how the argument played out. <br />The moment where the Fool tells Fitz that his love for him has no limitations my heart broke. The Fool is utterly in love Fitz, and while Fitz loves the Fool he is angered and a little disgusted by the revelation. The Fool has never brought up his true feelings because he knows that Fitz does reciprocate them. He would never put Fitz in that position, he knows it would alter their friendship for ever. <br />I hated how Fitz spoke to the Fool in this chapter. Although I understand Fitz's need to know how the Fool feels about him, I think he showed no regard for the Fools feelings. Considering how close they both are he should have known better. Also, Fitz had an inkling about it, he should have been prepared for the possibility that the Fool was in love with him. He had eavesdropped on the conversation that Fool had with Jek. <br />After the argument the Fool remains only as Lord Golden. He retreats into the safety of that character and will only talk to Fitz as Lord Golden. Not the Fool. And even when he does speak, it is cold and unaffectionate. We only get to see glimpses of the Fool again when he shows Fitz his tattoo's and talks about the prophecy involving his death on the island with the dragon. <br /><br />That last couple of pages made me hopeful again that the Fitz and the Fool had made a bit of peace. Fitz calling Fool by his true name "Beloved" went a long way to apologising. <br /><br />Something else that I've been musing about today is the different characters that the Fool has. Fitz recognised this towards the end of the book, that Lord Golden, Amber and even Fool were all characters of his. Roles for him to play when he needs them. He has different personalities in each of these roles, all of them eccentric in their own ways. <br />But it struck me that another one of his characters is the White Prophet. Whenever he talks to Fitz about what they must do, prophecy, or Fools past, he takes on yet another personality. I think this one is his true personality. He's scared, he knows he has to use Fitz to his own ends. I don't think he feels comfortable in this. He even tells Fitz in this book that he doesn't want to be the White Prophet anymore. He can't go through another death of Fitz's. He also makes the least sense when his White Prophet and yet makes the most sense at the same time. The White Prophet is always sombre and a little hysterical, he doubts himself and yet knows that his prophecy will come true at some point. <br /><br />I have a feeling the last book in this trilogy is going to break my heart. We shall see if Fitz will stay loyal to the Farseer's or loyal to his Beloved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12319322312584607041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1381836090" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381836090" />
    <a title="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17825291-katie-ziegler-life-between-words"><img alt="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434161411p2/17825291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1381836090?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)" href="/user/show/17825291-katie-ziegler-life-between-words">Katie Ziegler (Life Between Words)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007585908" href="/book/show/23018984-the-golden-fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17825291-katie-ziegler-life-between-words?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1381836090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3318345079883210958">Can I give this book anything other than five stars? I have invested so much time and so many emotions with these characters. I know them so well now...all of their flaws and their humanity; they make mistakes and yet they still grow in wisdom. They feel so *real*. I LOVE THEM. <br/><br/>And as a sidenote, you can read the Fitz and the Fool books separately from her other Realm of the Elderlings series, but I don't suggest doing so. You'll get SO much more out of the world if you read them all in order. I</span>
  <span id="freeText3318345079883210958" style="display:none">Can I give this book anything other than five stars? I have invested so much time and so many emotions with these characters. I know them so well now...all of their flaws and their humanity; they make mistakes and yet they still grow in wisdom. They feel so *real*. I LOVE THEM. <br /><br />And as a sidenote, you can read the Fitz and the Fool books separately from her other Realm of the Elderlings series, but I don't suggest doing so. You'll get SO much more out of the world if you read them all in order. In this series, you meet up with characters that you know from the Liveship trilogy - you'll understand so much more if you go into this book with knowledge from the previous trilogy! <br /><br />This book did suffer from second book syndrome. It felt like the whole thing was setting us up for the last installment in the trilogy. It was NECESSARY setup, and interesting. But setup nonetheless. Still...I love the characters and the writing so much, I'm not bumping down the rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3318345079883210958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_202684532" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202684532" />
    <a title="Wastrel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel"><img alt="Wastrel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317660831p2/5743748.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/202684532?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wastrel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wastrel" href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel">Wastrel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007160389" href="/book/show/418506.The_Golden_Fool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=r-ss">r-ss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=z-2002">z-2002</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=fantastika-fantasy-saga">fantastika-fantasy-saga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202684532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13748492675261311747">It's hard to be objective, because this is one of my favourite books of all time. After seven volumes, we're now so deeply into the mind of FitzChivalry Farseer that it feels like a second home, and while some may complain that nothing whatsoever happens in this book (they'd be wrong - a lot <i>happens</i> in this book, there just isn't really a plot), I rejoiced in being given the time and space to see more of Fitz dealing with ordinary life. Hobb's great stylistic strength might be the way that she t</span>
  <span id="freeText13748492675261311747" style="display:none">It's hard to be objective, because this is one of my favourite books of all time. After seven volumes, we're now so deeply into the mind of FitzChivalry Farseer that it feels like a second home, and while some may complain that nothing whatsoever happens in this book (they'd be wrong - a lot <i>happens</i> in this book, there just isn't really a plot), I rejoiced in being given the time and space to see more of Fitz dealing with ordinary life. Hobb's great stylistic strength might be the way that she takes often quite cliche and uninteresting fantasy tropes and revitalises them, by showing what they mean for real people - what motivates the tropes, and what their consequences are.<br /><br />This is also that very rare thing, a grown-up fantasy novel, by grown-ups, about grown-ups, and to a larger extent for grown-ups, as the middle-aged Fitz looks on upon the foolish actions of younger characters (and it's great to see parental concern, one of life's greatest motivating forces, take centre stage in a fantasy novel, rather than romantic love, or adventure, or glory), and looks back upon his own youthful follies. But just as the young Fitz made a lot of mistakes, so too perhaps do the two middle-aged Fitzes (both the Fitz who is a character in the novel and the later Fitz who acts as the narrator) - but this flawed narrator is nothing more than an extension of the flawing, the humanity, of all the characters.<br /><br />I'm not going to go on at too much length. I suppose to sum it up, I would say: this is a great fantasy novel about relationships and psychology and growing older; it also has a surprising amount of dramatic tension, not only around the relationship developments but also around the inchoate heroic plotline that will take over in the final volume of the trilogy; it is, however, rather formless, with a lot of parallel plot strands but no overall arc, and consequently the emotional pacing is lacking and there is no fulfilling climax (or there is, or are, but it or they are long before the end); it definitely benefits from the reader having read The Liveship Traders as well as The Farseer Trilogy; if you don't like Fitz, you won't like this book; if you love Fitz, hopefully you'll love this book.<br /><br /><a href="http://vacuouswastrel.wordpress.com/2013/02/04/the-golden-fool-by-robin-hobb/" rel="nofollow noopener">I go on (and on) at greater length about the book over on my blog, HERE.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13748492675261311747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1211757723" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Dara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13656026-dara"><img alt="Dara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500476380p2/13656026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=series">series</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13656026-dara?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211757723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer346344846328848748">It's getting more and more difficult for me to articulate what I love about these books. It's a combination of so many things. Fitz has become one of my all-time favorite characters, along with many of his friends. The world of the Elderlings is endlessly fascinating. There's a deep history there - in the Six Duchies and beyond - that I want to know about. The magic in this series is captivating and mysterious - I always want to experience more of the Skill and the Wit. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb' title='Robin Hobb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robin Hobb</a>'s writing is m</span>
  <span id="freeText346344846328848748" style="display:none">It's getting more and more difficult for me to articulate what I love about these books. It's a combination of so many things. Fitz has become one of my all-time favorite characters, along with many of his friends. The world of the Elderlings is endlessly fascinating. There's a deep history there - in the Six Duchies and beyond - that I want to know about. The magic in this series is captivating and mysterious - I always want to experience more of the Skill and the Wit. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a>'s writing is masterful and emotional. I really can't get enough.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45109.Golden_Fool__Tawny_Man___2_" title="Golden Fool (Tawny Man, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Golden Fool</a> continues where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45108.Fool_s_Fate__Tawny_Man___3_" title="Fool's Fate (Tawny Man, #3) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool's Fate</a> left off. <i>Golden Fool</i>deals more with Fitz's relationships than any plots against the Farseer throne. Fitz gets closer to Price Dutiful, he becomes wiser about Chade's nature, he makes mistakes when it comes to romance, and his and the Fool's relationship undergo a few changes. <br /> <br />I wanted more answers in the Farseer trilogy about the Skill and how it works. I finally have some answers. There's a lot more exploration of that magic in this book with less focus on Wit magic.<br /><br />First-person POV is my least favorite to read. More often than not, the view is too limited to immerse me in the world of the main character. That's not the case here. Again, Hobb is Queen of all Things. I never feel like things are diminished because I only see them through Fitz's eyes.<br /><br />I'm getting the feeling that I got after finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45101.The_Mad_Ship__Liveship_Traders___2_" title="The Mad Ship (Liveship Traders, #2) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mad Ship</a> - I can't wait to read the next book but I don't want the story to end. <br /><br /><b>A+</b></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sbR1/5MCabTd9ycEGgTOsDOb31LUkNE+cVQQHbf3veeLkhwtKFyg3Hrck2Xt8cRv5cQ4mhodX1kqKlaserRPfQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aRl45i/QIB1bMjJs7n2PnJ5H/R9se51C94RszhrsqwBTPxE0lI7pdfwZhg0ZiIVDSBga16L2EyWs+ip/169Zmg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">About Robin Hobb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1397885202p3/25307.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">Robin Hobb

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13325292246940823146">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText13325292246940823146" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>

There they must fulfil the Narcheska\'s challenge to her betrothed: to lay the head of the dragon Icefyre, whom legends tell is buried there deep beneath the ice, upon her hearth.
